<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span></h2>
<p>Netflix's <a href="/wiki/Video_on_demand" title="Video on demand">video on demand</a> streaming service, formerly branded as <i>Watch Now</i>, allows subscribers to stream television series and films via the Netflix website on <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">personal computers</a>, or the Netflix software on a variety of supported platforms, including <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Digital_media_player" title="Digital media player">digital media players</a>, <a href="/wiki/Video_game_console" title="Video game console">video game consoles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smart_TV" title="Smart TV">smart TVs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> According to a <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_N.V." class="mw-redirect" title="Nielsen N.V.">Nielsen</a> survey in July 2011, 42% of Netflix users used a standalone computer, 25% used the <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a>, 14% by connecting computers to a television, 13% with a <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a> and 12% an <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When the streaming service first launched, Netflix's disc rental subscribers were given access at no additional charge. Subscribers were allowed approximately one hour of streaming per dollar spent on the monthly subscription (a $16.99 plan, for example, entitled the subscriber to 17 hours of streaming media). In January 2008, however, Netflix lifted this restriction, at which point virtually all rental-disc subscribers became entitled to unlimited streaming at no additional cost (however, subscribers on the restricted plan of two DVDs per month ($4.99) remained limited to two hours of streaming per month). This change came in a response to the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Hulu" title="Hulu">Hulu</a> and to <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>'s new video-rental services.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Netflix later split DVD rental subscriptions and streaming subscriptions into separate, standalone services, at which point the monthly caps on Internet streaming were lifted.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Netflix service plans are currently divided into three price tiers; the lowest offers <a href="/wiki/Standard_definition" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard definition">standard definition</a> streaming on a single device, the second allows <a href="/wiki/High_definition_television" class="mw-redirect" title="High definition television">high definition</a> streaming on two devices simultaneously, and the "Platinum" tier allows simultaneous streaming on up to four devices, and <a href="/wiki/4K_resolution" title="4K resolution">4K</a> streaming on supported devices and Internet connections. The HD subscription plan historically cost US$7.99; in April 2014, Netflix announced that it would raise the price of this plan to $9.99 for new subscribers, but that existing customers would be grandfathered under this older price until May 2016, after which they could downgrade to the SD-only tier at the same price, or pay the higher fee for continued high definition access.<sup id="cite_ref-cbc-nflxprices_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc-nflxprices-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cbc-newtiers_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc-newtiers-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-verge-4kprice_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-4kprice-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2016, a Netflix subscriber sued the company over the price increases, alleging he was told by a Netflix customer support representative in 2011 that they would pay the same price in perpetuity as long as they maintained their subscription continuously.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On November 30, 2016, Netflix launched an offline playback feature, allowing users of the Netflix mobile apps on Android or iOS to cache content on their devices in standard or high quality for viewing without an Internet connection. The feature is primarily available on selected series and films, and Netflix stated that more content would be supported by the feature over time.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-verge-offlinenetflix_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-offlinenetflix-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Netflix will partner with airlines to provide them with its mobile streaming technology. This will start in early 2018 as part of an effort to get airlines to provide better in-flight Wi-Fi.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018 Netflix introduced the "Skip Intro" feature which allows customers to skip the intros to shows on its platform. They do so through a variety of techniques including manual reviewing, audio tagging, and machine learning.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (May 2019)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marc_Randolph_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Marc_Randolph_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/220px-Marc_Randolph_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Marc_Randolph_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/330px-Marc_Randolph_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Marc_Randolph_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/440px-Marc_Randolph_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4296" data-file-height="3700" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marc_Randolph_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marc Randolph, co-founder of Netflix and the first CEO of the company</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Reed_Hastings,_Web_2.0_Conference.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Reed_Hastings%2C_Web_2.0_Conference.jpg/220px-Reed_Hastings%2C_Web_2.0_Conference.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="319" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Reed_Hastings%2C_Web_2.0_Conference.jpg/330px-Reed_Hastings%2C_Web_2.0_Conference.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Reed_Hastings%2C_Web_2.0_Conference.jpg/440px-Reed_Hastings%2C_Web_2.0_Conference.jpg 2x" data-file-width="690" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Reed_Hastings,_Web_2.0_Conference.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Reed Hastings, co-founder and the current Chairman and CEO</div></div></div>
<p>On October 1, 2008, Netflix announced a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Starz_Inc." title="Starz Inc.">Starz</a> to bring 2,500+ new films and shows to "Watch Instantly", under Starz Play.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2010, Netflix reached a five-year deal worth nearly $1 billion to stream films from <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">Paramount</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lionsgate" title="Lionsgate">Lionsgate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer</a>. The deal increased Netflix's annual spending fees, adding roughly $200 million per year. It spent $117 million in the first six months of 2010 on streaming, up from $31 million in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
On July 12, 2011, Netflix announced that it would separate its existing subscription plans into two separate plans: one covering the streaming and the other DVD rental services.<sup id="cite_ref-cnet_hike_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnet_hike-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> The cost for streaming would be $7.99 per month, while DVD rental would start at the same price. The announcement led to panned reception amongst Netflix's Facebook followers, who posted negative comments on its wall.<sup id="cite_ref-cnet_negative_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnet_negative-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> comments spiked a negative "Dear Netflix" trend.<sup id="cite_ref-cnet_negative_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnet_negative-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> The company defended its decision during its initial announcement of the change:</p><blockquote><p>"Given the long life we think DVDs by mail will have, treating DVDs as a $2 add-on to our unlimited streaming plan neither makes great financial sense nor satisfies people who just want DVDs. Creating an unlimited-DVDs-by-mail plan (no streaming) at our lowest price ever, $7.99, does make sense and will ensure a long life for our DVDs-by-mail offering."<sup id="cite_ref-cnet_hike_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnet_hike-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote><p>In a reversal, Netflix announced in October that its streaming and DVD-rental plans would remain branded together.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2018, Netflix named Spencer Neumann as the new CFO.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disc_rental">Disc rental</span></h3>
<p>In the United States, the company provides a monthly <a href="/wiki/Flat_rate" title="Flat rate">flat-fee</a> for DVD and <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray" title="Blu-ray">Blu-ray</a> rentals. A subscriber creates a rental queue, a list, of films to rent. The films are delivered individually via the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">United States Postal Service</a> from regional <a href="/wiki/Warehouse" title="Warehouse">warehouses</a>. As of March 28, 2011, Netflix had 58 shipping locations throughout the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The subscriber can keep the rented disc as long as desired, but there is a limit on the number of discs that each subscriber can have simultaneously via different tiers. To rent a new disc, the subscriber must return the previous disc in a <a href="/wiki/Metered_reply_mail" title="Metered reply mail">metered reply mail</a> envelope. Upon receipt, Netflix ships the next available disc in the subscriber's rental queue.
</p><p>Netflix offers pricing tiers for DVD rental. On November 21, 2008, Netflix began offering subscribers rentals on <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_disc" class="mw-redirect" title="Blu-ray disc">Blu-ray disc</a> for an additional fee. In addition, Netflix sold used discs, delivered and billed identically as rentals. This service was discontinued at the end of November.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 6, 2010, Netflix agreed with <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> to delay new release rentals 28 days prior to retail, in an attempt to help studios sell physical copies, with similar deals involving <a href="/wiki/Universal_Pictures" title="Universal Pictures">Universal</a> and <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a> were reached on April 9.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, Netflix split its service pricing. Currently, Netflix's disc rental memberships range from $7.99 to $19.99/m, including a free one-month trial and unlimited DVD exchanges.
</p><p>On September 18, 2011, Netflix announced that it would split out and rebrand its DVD-by-mail service as Qwikster. CEO Reed Hastings justified the decision, stating that "we realized that streaming and DVD by mail are becoming two quite different businesses, with very different cost structures, different benefits that need to be marketed differently, and we need to let each grow and operate independently." It was also announced that the re-branded service would add video game rentals. The decision to split the services was widely criticized; it was noted that the two websites would have been autonomous from each other (with ratings, reviews, and queues not carrying over between them), and would have required separate user accounts. Also, the two websites would require separate subscriptions.<sup id="cite_ref-fastco-splitqwik_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fastco-splitqwik-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tc-qwikster_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tc-qwikster-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt-deathsprial_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-deathsprial-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnnmoney-abandoned_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnnmoney-abandoned-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 10, 2011, Netflix announced that it had shelved the planned re-branding in response to customer feedback and after the stock price plummeted nearly 30%, and that the DVD-by-mail and streaming services would continue to operate through a single website under the Netflix brand. Netflix stated that it had lost 800,000 subscribers in the fourth quarter of 2011—a loss partially credited to the poor reception of the aborted re-branding.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-deathsprial_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-deathsprial-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnnmoney-abandoned_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnnmoney-abandoned-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt-lostgoodwill_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-lostgoodwill-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2012, Netflix confirmed to <i><a href="/wiki/TechCrunch" title="TechCrunch">TechCrunch</a></i> that it had acquired the <a href="/wiki/Domain_name" title="Domain name">domain name</a> DVD.com. By 2016, Netflix had quietly rebranded its DVD-by-mail service under the name <i>DVD.com, A Netflix Company</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-motleyfool-dvdcom_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-motleyfool-dvdcom-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tc-dvdcom_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tc-dvdcom-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-paste-envelope_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paste-envelope-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2017, the service still has 3.3 million customers, and Hastings plans to keep it for at least five more years.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The first quarter of 2018, DVD rentals gave $60.2 million profit from $120.4 million in revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Profiles">Profiles</span></h3>
<p>In June 2008, Netflix announced plans to eliminate its online subscriber profile feature.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Profiles allow one subscriber account to contain multiple users (for example, a couple, two roommates, or parent and child) with separate DVD queues, ratings, recommendations, friend lists, reviews, and intra-site communications for each. Netflix contended that elimination of profiles would improve the customer experience.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> However, likely as a result of negative reviews and reaction by Netflix users,<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Netflix reversed its decision to remove profiles 11 days after the announcement.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> In announcing the reinstatement of profiles, Netflix defended its original decision, stating, "Because of an ongoing desire to make our website easier to use, we believed taking a feature away that is only used by a very small minority would help us improve the site for everyone," then explained its reversal: "Listening to our members, we realized that users of this feature often describe it as an essential part of their Netflix experience. Simplicity is only one virtue and it can certainly be outweighed by utility."<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Reintroduction">Reintroduction</span></h4>
<p>Netflix reinvigorated the "Profiles" feature on August 1, 2013, that permits accounts to accommodate up to five user profiles, associated either with individuals or thematic occasions. "Profiles" effectively divides the interest of each user, so that each will receive individualized suggestions and adding favorites individually. "This is important", according to Todd Yellin, Netflix's Vice President of Product Innovation, because, "About 75 percent to 80 percent of what people watch on Netflix comes from what Netflix recommends, not from what people search for".<sup id="cite_ref-author=Stenovec_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-author=Stenovec-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Moreover, Mike McGuire, a VP at <a href="/wiki/Gartner_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Gartner Group">Gartner</a>, said: "profiles will give Netflix even more detailed information about its subscribers and their viewing habits, allowing the company to make better decisions about what movies and TV shows to offer".<sup id="cite_ref-author=Stenovec,_Timothy_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-author=Stenovec,_Timothy-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, profiles lets users link their individual <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> accounts, and thus share individual watch queues and recommendations,<sup id="cite_ref-author=Stenovec,_Timothy_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-author=Stenovec,_Timothy-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pepitone,_Julianne_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pepitone,_Julianne-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> since its addition in March after lobbying Congress to change an outdated act.<sup id="cite_ref-Pepitone,_Julianne_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pepitone,_Julianne-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Neil Hunt, Netflix's former Chief Product Officer, told <a href="/wiki/CNNMoney" class="mw-redirect" title="CNNMoney">CNNMoney</a>: "profiles are another way to stand out in the crowded streaming-video space", and, "The company said <a href="/wiki/Focus_group" title="Focus group">focus-group</a> testing showed that profiles generate more viewing and more engagement".<sup id="cite_ref-money.cnn.com_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-money.cnn.com-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hunt says Netflix may link profiles to specific devices, in time, so a subscriber can skip the step of launching a specific profile each time s/he logs into Netflix on a given device.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawler_Profiles_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawler_Profiles-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Critics of the feature have noted:
</p>
<ul><li>New profiles are created as "blank slates",<sup id="cite_ref-Lawler_Profiles_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawler_Profiles-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> but viewing history prior to profile creations stays profile-wide.<sup id="cite_ref-Rogowsky_Steps_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rogowsky_Steps-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>People don't always watch Netflix alone, and media watched with viewing partner(s) – whose tastes might not reflect the owner(s) – affect recommendations made to that profile.<sup id="cite_ref-money.cnn.com_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-money.cnn.com-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lawler_Profiles_160-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawler_Profiles-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rogowsky_Steps_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rogowsky_Steps-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>In response to both concerns, however, users can refine future recommendations for a given profile by rating the shows watched and by their ongoing viewing habits.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawler_Profiles_160-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawler_Profiles-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rogowsky_Steps_161-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rogowsky_Steps-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsidiaries">Subsidiaries</span></h3>
<ul><li>DVD.com – Rents DVDs by mail</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Millarworld" title="Millarworld">Millarworld</a> – A comic book company that was founded in 2004 by <a href="/wiki/Scottish_national_identity" title="Scottish national identity">Scottish</a> <a href="/wiki/Comic_book" title="Comic book">comic book</a> <a href="/wiki/Writer" title="Writer">writer</a> <a href="/wiki/Mark_Millar" title="Mark Millar">Mark Millar</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Creator_ownership" class="mw-redirect" title="Creator ownership">creator-owned</a> line.</li>
<li>Netflix Pte. Ltd. – Netflix's studio in Singapore.</li>
<li>Netflix Services UK Limited – A British division that holds Private limited with Share Capital.</li>
<li>Netflix Streaming Services International B.V. – A Netflix subsidiary in the Netherlands.</li>
<li>Netflix Streaming Services, Inc. – A subsidiary that license and streams all of Netflix's films and shows.</li>
<li>Netflix Global, LLC – A Foreign Limited-Liability Company filed on August 3, 2016, that co-produces all foreign programming and films</li>
<li>Netflix Studios – A film and television studio that co-produces any original or foreign content.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Netflix Services Germany GmbH – A studio that contributes to German film subsidies supporting domestic movie and TV production in the country.</li>
<li>NetflixCS, Inc. – Another located 1108 E SOUTH UNION AVE Midvale, UT 84047  (Mid-Atlantic U.S.).</li>
<li>Netflix Luxembourg S.a r.l. – A subsidiary located in Luxembourg, Europe.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products">Products</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Netflix_button.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Netflix_button.jpg/220px-Netflix_button.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Netflix_button.jpg/330px-Netflix_button.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Netflix_button.jpg/440px-Netflix_button.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Netflix_button.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Aquos" class="mw-redirect" title="Aquos">Aquos</a> <a href="/wiki/Remote_control" title="Remote control">remote control</a> with a Netflix button</div></div></div>
<p>In 2007, Netflix recruited one of the early <a href="/wiki/Digital_video_recorder" title="Digital video recorder">DVR</a> business pioneers <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Wood_(businessman)" title="Anthony Wood (businessman)">Anthony Wood</a> to build a "Netflix Player" that would allow streaming content to be played directly on a television set rather than a PC or laptop.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> While the player was initially developed at Netflix, Reed Hastings eventually shut down the project to help encourage other hardware manufacturers to include built-in Netflix support.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Wood eventually launched the player as the first device from <a href="/wiki/Roku,_Inc." title="Roku, Inc.">Roku Inc.</a> which is now primarily known for its streaming video players, with Netflix serving as a primary investor in the new company.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, Netflix introduced a Netflix button for certain <a href="/wiki/Remote_control" title="Remote control">remote controls</a>, allowing users to instantly access Netflix on compatible devices.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Netflix revealed a prototype of the new device called "The Switch" at the 2015 World <a href="/wiki/Maker_Faire" title="Maker Faire">Maker Faire</a> New York. "The Switch" allows Netflix users to turn off lights when connected to a smart home light system. It also connects to users' local networks to enable their servers to order takeout, and silence one's phone at the press of a button. Though the device hasn't been patented, Netflix released instructions on their website, on how to build it at home (DIY). The instructions cover both the electrical structure and the programming processes.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2015, the company received significant technical support from France's <a href="/wiki/CNRS" class="mw-redirect" title="CNRS">CNRS</a> concerning video compression and formating, through CNRS' Laboratoire des Sciences du Numérique de Nantes (LS2N). In March 2017 at Barcelona's World Congress for mobile technologies, the American company presented the French lab's <a href="/wiki/Open_source_technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Open source technology">open-source technological</a> creation: a compression tool allowing HD+ video quality with a bandwidth need of under 100 <a href="/wiki/Octet_(computing)" title="Octet (computing)">kilo octets</a> per second, 40 times less than that of HD TV needs and compatible with mobile services worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2016, Netflix created a new tool called FAST to determine the speed of an Internet connection.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Content">Content</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Original_programming">Original programming</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_original_programs_distributed_by_Netflix" title="List of original programs distributed by Netflix">List of original programs distributed by Netflix</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_original_films_distributed_by_Netflix" title="List of original films distributed by Netflix">List of original films distributed by Netflix</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_original_stand-up_comedy_specials_distributed_by_Netflix" title="List of original stand-up comedy specials distributed by Netflix">List of original stand-up comedy specials distributed by Netflix</a></div>
<p>A "<a href="/wiki/List_of_original_programs_distributed_by_Netflix" title="List of original programs distributed by Netflix">Netflix Original</a>" is content that is produced, co-produced, or distributed by Netflix exclusively on their services. Netflix funds their original shows differently than other TV networks when they sign a project, providing the money upfront and immediately ordering two seasons of most series.<sup id="cite_ref-hr-backlash_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hr-backlash-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2011, Netflix began acquiring original content for its library, beginning with the hour-long political drama <i><a href="/wiki/House_of_Cards_(U.S._TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Cards (U.S. TV series)">House of Cards</a></i>, which debuted in February 2013. The series was produced by <a href="/wiki/David_Fincher" title="David Fincher">David Fincher</a>, and starred <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Spacey" title="Kevin Spacey">Kevin Spacey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> In late 2011, Netflix picked up two eight-episode seasons of <i><a href="/wiki/Lilyhammer" title="Lilyhammer">Lilyhammer</a></i> and a fourth season of the ex-<a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a> sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/Arrested_Development_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Arrested Development (TV series)">Arrested Development</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Netflix released the supernatural drama series <i><a href="/wiki/Hemlock_Grove_(TV_series)" title="Hemlock Grove (TV series)">Hemlock Grove</a></i> in early 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline-4643325_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline-4643325-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2013, DreamWorks Animation and Netflix co-produced <i><a href="/wiki/Turbo_Fast" title="Turbo Fast">Turbo Fast</a></i>, based on the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Turbo_(film)" title="Turbo (film)">Turbo</a></i>, which premiered in July.<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline-614048_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline-614048-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Deadline-7591984_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline-7591984-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Netflix has since become a major distributor of <a href="/wiki/List_of_original_programs_distributed_by_Netflix#Children_and_family" title="List of original programs distributed by Netflix">animated family and kid shows</a>.
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Orange_Is_the_New_Black" title="Orange Is the New Black">Orange Is the New Black</a></i> debuted on the streaming service in July 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> In a rare discussion of a Netflix show's ratings, Netflix executives have commented that the show is Netflix's most-watched original series.<sup id="cite_ref-Ha_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ha-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rating_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rating-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> In February 2016, <i>Orange Is the New Black</i> was renewed for a fifth, sixth and seventh season. On June 9, 2017, season 5 was premiered and the sixth season premiered on July 27, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2013, Netflix and <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Television" title="Marvel Television">Marvel Television</a> announced a five-season deal to produce live-action Marvel superhero-focused series: <a href="/wiki/Daredevil_(Marvel_Comics_character)" title="Daredevil (Marvel Comics character)">Daredevil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Jones" title="Jessica Jones">Jessica Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iron_Fist_(comics)" title="Iron Fist (comics)">Iron Fist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luke_Cage" title="Luke Cage">Luke Cage</a>. The deal involves the release of four 13-episode seasons that culminate in a mini-series called <i><a href="/wiki/Defenders_(comics)" title="Defenders (comics)">The Defenders</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Daredevil_(TV_series)" title="Daredevil (TV series)"><i>Daredevil</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Jones_(TV_series)" title="Jessica Jones (TV series)"><i>Jessica Jones</i></a> premiered in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Netflix_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Netflix-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Luke_Cage_(TV_series)" title="Luke Cage (TV series)">Luke Cage</a></i> series premiered on September 30, 2016, followed by <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Fist_(TV_series)" title="Iron Fist (TV series)">Iron Fist</a></i> on March 17, 2017, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Defenders_(miniseries)" title="The Defenders (miniseries)">The Defenders</a></i> on August 18, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> In April 2016, the Netflix series in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_television_series" title="List of Marvel Cinematic Universe television series">Marvel Cinematic Universe</a> were expanded further, to include a 13-episode series of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Punisher_(TV_series)" title="The Punisher (TV series)">The Punisher</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-PunisherEWApr2016_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PunisherEWApr2016-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PunisherEpCount_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PunisherEpCount-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> In addition to the Marvel deal, Disney announced that the television series <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars_(2008_TV_series)" title="Star Wars: The Clone Wars (2008 TV series)">Star Wars: The Clone Wars</a></i> would release its sixth and final season on Netflix, as well as all five prior and the <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars_(film)" title="Star Wars: The Clone Wars (film)">feature film</a>. The new <i>Star Wars</i> content was released on Netflix's streaming service on March 7, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-C4Wauto-4596604_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C4Wauto-4596604-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2014, Netflix signed <i>Arrested Development</i> creator <a href="/wiki/Mitchell_Hurwitz" title="Mitchell Hurwitz">Mitch Hurwitz</a> and his production firm The Hurwitz Company to a multi-year deal to create original projects for the service.<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline-5977108_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline-5977108-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Historical_period_drama" title="Historical period drama">period drama</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo_(TV_series)" title="Marco Polo (TV series)">Marco Polo</a></i> premiered on December 12, 2014. The animated sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/BoJack_Horseman" title="BoJack Horseman">BoJack Horseman</a></i> premiered in August 2014, to mixed reviews on release but garnering wide critical acclaim for the following seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The science fiction drama <i><a href="/wiki/Sense8" title="Sense8">Sense8</a></i> debuted in June 2015, which was written and produced by <a href="/wiki/The_Wachowskis" title="The Wachowskis">The Wachowskis</a> and <a href="/wiki/J._Michael_Straczynski" title="J. Michael Straczynski">J. Michael Straczynski</a><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Bloodline_(TV_series)" title="Bloodline (TV series)">Bloodline</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Narcos" title="Narcos">Narcos</a></i> were two other drama series that Netflix released in 2015. On November 6, 2015, <i><a href="/wiki/Master_of_None" title="Master of None">Master of None</a></i> premiered, starring <a href="/wiki/Aziz_Ansari" title="Aziz Ansari">Aziz Ansari</a>. Other comedy shows premiering in 2015 included <i><a href="/wiki/Unbreakable_Kimmy_Schmidt" title="Unbreakable Kimmy Schmidt">Unbreakable Kimmy Schmidt</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Grace_and_Frankie" title="Grace and Frankie">Grace and Frankie</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Wet_Hot_American_Summer:_First_Day_of_Camp" title="Wet Hot American Summer: First Day of Camp">Wet Hot American Summer: First Day of Camp</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/W/_Bob_%26_David" title="W/ Bob &amp; David">W/ Bob &amp; David</a></i>.
</p><p>Netflix continued to dramatically expand their original content in 2016. The <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">science fiction</a> <a href="/wiki/Horror_fiction" title="Horror fiction">horror</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Stranger_Things" title="Stranger Things">Stranger Things</a></i> premiered in July 2016, music-driven drama <i><a href="/wiki/The_Get_Down" title="The Get Down">The Get Down</a></i> in August, historical drama <i><a href="/wiki/The_Crown_(TV_series)" title="The Crown (TV series)">The Crown</a></i> in November, and the year's premieres included comedy shows such as <i><a href="/wiki/Love_(TV_series)" title="Love (TV series)">Love</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Flaked" title="Flaked">Flaked</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Netflix_Presents:_The_Characters" title="Netflix Presents: The Characters">Netflix Presents: The Characters</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ranch_(TV_series)" title="The Ranch (TV series)">The Ranch</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Lady_Dynamite_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lady Dynamite (TV series)">Lady Dynamite</a></i>. Netflix released an estimated 126 original series or films in 2016, more than any other network or cable channel.<sup id="cite_ref-hr-backlash_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hr-backlash-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 14, 2016, Netflix and <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a> jointly acquired the U.S distribution rights to the Canadian <a href="/wiki/Independent_film" title="Independent film">independent</a> <a href="/wiki/Drama_(film_and_television)" title="Drama (film and television)">drama film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Two_Lovers_and_a_Bear" title="Two Lovers and a Bear">Two Lovers and a Bear</a></i> following its screening at the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="Toronto International Film Festival">Toronto International Film Festival</a> on September 9, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Netflix has also invested in distributing exclusive stand-up comedy specials from such notable comedians as <a href="/wiki/Dave_Chappelle" title="Dave Chappelle">Dave Chappelle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louis_C.K." title="Louis C.K.">Louis C.K.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Rock" title="Chris Rock">Chris Rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Gaffigan" title="Jim Gaffigan">Jim Gaffigan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Burr" title="Bill Burr">Bill Burr</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Seinfeld" title="Jerry Seinfeld">Jerry Seinfeld</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> In January 2017, Netflix announced all Seinfeld's <i><a href="/wiki/Comedians_in_Cars_Getting_Coffee" title="Comedians in Cars Getting Coffee">Comedians in Cars Getting Coffee</a></i> episodes and season 10 would be on their service.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The company has started internally self-producing its original content, such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ranch_(TV_series)" title="The Ranch (TV series)">The Ranch</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Chelsea_(TV_series)" title="Chelsea (TV series)">Chelsea</a></i>, through its Netflix Studios production house.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Netflix expected to release 1,000 hours of original content in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2017, Netflix iterated a goal of having half of its library consist of original content by 2019, announcing a plan to invest $8 billion on original content in 2018. There will be a particular focus on films and <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a> through this investment, with a plan to produce 80 original films and 30 anime series.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> In September 2017, <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Heritage" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister of Heritage">Minister of Heritage</a> <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9lanie_Joly" title="Mélanie Joly">Mélanie Joly</a> also announced that Netflix had agreed to make a <a href="/wiki/Canadian_dollar" title="Canadian dollar">CDN$</a>500 million (US$400 million) investment over the next five years in the production of content in Canada. The company denied that the deal was intended to result in a <a href="/wiki/Tax_break" title="Tax break">tax break</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> A study found that Netflix had realized this goal by December 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2017, Netflix announced that it would be making its first original Colombian series, to be executive produced by <a href="/wiki/Ciro_Guerra" title="Ciro Guerra">Ciro Guerra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2018, chief content officer Ted Sarandos stated that Netflix had increased its spending on original content, with 85% of its new content spending that year being devoted to it.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 31, 2018, a concert film of Taylor Swift's <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift%27s_Reputation_Stadium_Tour" title="Taylor Swift&#39;s Reputation Stadium Tour">Reputation tour</a> was released on Netflix.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2019, <a href="/wiki/Gwyneth_Paltrow" title="Gwyneth Paltrow">Gwyneth Paltrow</a>'s lifestyle brand <a href="/wiki/Goop_(company)" title="Goop (company)">Goop</a> signed a deal to produce a wellness-themed docuseries for Netflix.<sup id="cite_ref-ars-goopseries_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-goopseries-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_television_deals">Film and television deals</span></h3>
<p>Netflix currently has exclusive <a href="/wiki/Pay_television" title="Pay television">pay TV</a> deals with several studios. The pay TV deals give Netflix exclusive streaming rights while adhering to the structures of traditional pay TV terms. Netflix's United States library includes newer releases from <a href="/wiki/Relativity_Media" title="Relativity Media">Relativity Media</a> and its subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Rogue_Pictures" title="Rogue Pictures">Rogue Pictures</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/DreamWorks_Animation" title="DreamWorks Animation">DreamWorks Animation</a><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> (until May 2018, when the studio signed a new contract with <a href="/wiki/Hulu" title="Hulu">Hulu</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Open_Road_Films" title="Open Road Films">Open Road Films</a><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> (though this deal expired in 2017; <a href="/wiki/Showtime_(TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Showtime (TV channel)">Showtime</a> has assumed pay television rights<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>), <a href="/wiki/Universal_Animation" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Animation">Universal Animation</a> (for animated films declined by <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a>), <a href="/wiki/FilmDistrict" title="FilmDistrict">FilmDistrict</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Weinstein_Company" title="The Weinstein Company">The Weinstein Company</a> (one of whose founders, <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Weinstein" title="Harvey Weinstein">Harvey Weinstein</a>, has been accused of sexual harassment as of 2017 (see <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Weinstein_sexual_abuse_allegations" title="Harvey Weinstein sexual abuse allegations">Harvey Weinstein sexual abuse allegations</a>), causing Netflix to withdraw from hosting the <a href="/wiki/75th_Golden_Globe_Awards" title="75th Golden Globe Awards">75th Golden Globe Awards</a> with TWC, and ending its Golden Globes partnership with the mini-major film studio<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>),<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Animation" title="Sony Pictures Animation">Sony Pictures Animation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" title="Walt Disney Studios (division)">Walt Disney Studios</a> (until 2019) catalog.
</p><p>Other distributors who have licensed content to Netflix include Warner Bros., Universal Pictures, <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Sony Pictures Entertainment">Sony Pictures Entertainment</a> and The Walt Disney Studios (including 20th Century Fox). Netflix also holds current and back-catalog rights to television programs distributed by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Television" title="Walt Disney Television">Walt Disney Television</a>, <a href="/wiki/DreamWorks_Classics" title="DreamWorks Classics">DreamWorks Classics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kino_International_(company)" title="Kino International (company)">Kino International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Television" title="Warner Bros. Television">Warner Bros. Television</a> and <a href="/wiki/CBS_Television_Distribution" title="CBS Television Distribution">CBS Television Distribution</a>, along with titles from other companies such as <a href="/wiki/Hasbro_Studios" class="mw-redirect" title="Hasbro Studios">Hasbro Studios</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saban_Capital_Group" title="Saban Capital Group">Saban Brands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Funimation" title="Funimation">Funimation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Viz_Media" title="Viz Media">Viz Media</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Viz_Media.com_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Viz_Media.com-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> Formerly, the streaming service also held rights to select television programs distributed by <a href="/wiki/NBCUniversal_Television_Distribution" title="NBCUniversal Television Distribution">NBCUniversal Television Distribution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Television" title="Sony Pictures Television">Sony Pictures Television</a> and <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox_Television" title="20th Century Fox Television">20th Century Fox Television</a>. Netflix also previously held the rights to select titles from vintage re-distributor <a href="/wiki/The_Criterion_Collection" title="The Criterion Collection">The Criterion Collection</a>, but these titles were pulled from Netflix and added to <a href="/wiki/Hulu" title="Hulu">Hulu</a>'s library.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> One of the more significant acquisitions was for the show <i><a href="/wiki/Breaking_Bad" title="Breaking Bad">Breaking Bad</a></i>, produced by Sony Pictures Television. Netflix acquired the rights after the show's third season in 2010, at a point where original broadcaster <a href="/wiki/AMC_(TV_channel)" title="AMC (TV channel)">AMC</a> had expressed the possibility of cancelling the show. Sony pushed Netflix to release <i>Breaking Bad</i> in time for the fourth season, which as a result, greatly expanded the show's audience on AMC due to new viewers binging on the Netflix past episodes, and doubling the viewership by the time of the fifth season. <i>Breaking Bad</i> is considered the first such show to have this "Netflix effect".<sup id="cite_ref-thr_20190918_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thr_20190918-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Epix_(TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Epix (TV channel)">Epix</a> signed a five-year streaming deal with Netflix. For the initial two years of this agreement, first-run and back-catalog content from Epix was exclusive to Netflix. Epix films would come to Netflix 90 days after their premiere on Epix. However, the exclusivity clause ended on September 4, 2012, when <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon</a> signed a deal with Epix to distribute its titles via the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Video" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Video">Amazon Video</a> streaming service.<sup id="cite_ref-C4Wauto-6307406_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C4Wauto-6307406-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> These include films from Paramount, Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer and Lionsgate.<sup id="cite_ref-USAToday-7407027_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-7407027-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters-8762026_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-8762026-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 1, 2011, <a href="/wiki/Starz_(TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Starz (TV channel)">Starz</a> ceased talks with Netflix to renew their streaming arrangement. As a result, Starz's library of films and series were removed from Netflix on February 28, 2012. Titles available on DVD were not affected and can still be acquired from Netflix via their <a href="/wiki/DVD-by-mail" title="DVD-by-mail">DVD-by-mail</a> service.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> However, select films broadcast on Starz continue to be available on Netflix under license from their respective television distributors.
</p><p>Netflix also negotiated to distribute animated films from Universal that HBO declined to acquire, such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lorax_(film)" title="The Lorax (film)">The Lorax</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/ParaNorman" title="ParaNorman">ParaNorman</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Minions_(film)" title="Minions (film)">Minions</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 23, 2012, Netflix and The Weinstein Company signed a multi-year output deal for RADiUS-TWC films.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, on December 4, Netflix and Disney announced an exclusive multi-year agreement for first-run United States subscription television rights to Walt Disney Studios' animated and live-action films, which were available on Netflix beginning in 2016. However, classics such as <i><a href="/wiki/Dumbo" title="Dumbo">Dumbo</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland_(1951_film)" title="Alice in Wonderland (1951 film)">Alice in Wonderland</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Pocahontas_(1995_film)" title="Pocahontas (1995 film)">Pocahontas</a></i> were instantly available upon completion of the deal.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Direct-to-video" title="Direct-to-video">Direct-to-video</a> releases were made available in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> The agreement with Disney is scheduled to end in 2019, as the company is preparing to launch a new streaming service that will carry all <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Studios" title="Marvel Studios">Marvel Studios</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lucasfilm" title="Lucasfilm">Lucasfilm</a> releases. Netflix will retain rights to continue streaming the Marvel series that were produced for the service.<sup id="cite_ref-cnet.com_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnet.com-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> With the <a href="/wiki/Proposed_acquisition_of_21st_Century_Fox_by_Disney" class="mw-redirect" title="Proposed acquisition of 21st Century Fox by Disney">Disney-Fox merger</a>, movie and TV titles from 20th Century Fox will likely follow suit after their deal with Netflix expires,<sup id="cite_ref-FoxDisneyPressRelease_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FoxDisneyPressRelease-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> except <i><a href="/wiki/Two_Lovers_and_a_Bear" title="Two Lovers and a Bear">Two Lovers and a Bear</a></i>, which Netflix will likely retain U.S streaming rights to as Fox and Netflix jointly acquired the U.S distribution rights to the film.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_192-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Time Warner CEO <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bewkes" title="Jeff Bewkes">Jeff Bewkes</a> in 2011 welcomed Netflix's ability to monetize older content that was previously not generating money for media companies.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> On January 14, 2013, Netflix signed an agreement with <a href="/wiki/WarnerMedia" title="WarnerMedia">Time Warner</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Turner_Broadcasting_System" title="Turner Broadcasting System">Turner Broadcasting System</a> and Warner Bros. Television to distribute <a href="/wiki/Cartoon_Network" title="Cartoon Network">Cartoon Network</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Animation" title="Warner Bros. Animation">Warner Bros. Animation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Adult_Swim" title="Adult Swim">Adult Swim</a> content, as well as <a href="/wiki/TNT_(U.S._TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="TNT (U.S. TV network)">TNT</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Dallas_(2012_TV_series)" title="Dallas (2012 TV series)">Dallas</a></i>, beginning in March 2013. The rights to these programs, previously held by Amazon Video, were given to Netflix shortly after their deal with <a href="/wiki/Viacom_(2005%E2%80%93present)" title="Viacom (2005–present)">Viacom</a> to stream <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon" title="Nickelodeon">Nickelodeon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nick_Jr." title="Nick Jr.">Nick Jr.</a> programs expired.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> However, Cartoon Network's ratings dropped by 10% in households that had Netflix, and so many of the shows from that channel and Adult Swim were removed in March 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-businessinsider.com_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-businessinsider.com-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> However, most of these shows were added to Hulu in May of the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-YouTube_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YouTube-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Canada, Netflix holds pay TV rights to films from Paramount, DreamWorks Animation and 20th Century Fox (shared with <a href="/wiki/The_Movie_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="The Movie Network">The Movie Network</a><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>), distributing all new content from those studios eight months after initial release. In 2015, the company also bought the Canadian pay TV rights to Disney films.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, opinion <a href="/wiki/Blog" title="Blog">blogger</a> Felix Salmon wrote that Netflix couldn't "afford the content that its subscribers most want to watch."<sup id="cite_ref-Algorithms_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Algorithms-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> He cited as evidence the company's loss of rights to stream several major movies. According to journalist Megan McArdle, the loss of these movies was extremely problematic for the company; specifically, she said that "[Netflix's] movie library is no longer actually a good substitute for a good movie rental place".<sup id="cite_ref-McArdle_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McArdle-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Netflix also began to acquire distribution rights to third-party films in 2017 into 2018. One of its first acquisitions was the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cloverfield_Paradox" title="The Cloverfield Paradox">The Cloverfield Paradox</a></i>, which Netflix had acquired from <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">Paramount Pictures</a> in early 2018, and launched on its service on February 4, 2018, shortly after airing its first trailer during <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LII" title="Super Bowl LII">Super Bowl LII</a>. While the film was critically panned, analysts believed that Netflix's purchase of the film helped to make the film instantly profitable for Paramount compared to a more traditional theatrical release, while Netflix benefited from the surprise reveal.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thr_cloverfield_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thr_cloverfield-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> Other films acquired by Netflix include international distribution for Paramount's <i><a href="/wiki/Annihilation_(film)" title="Annihilation (film)">Annihilation</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-thr_cloverfield_238-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thr_cloverfield-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> worldwide distribution of Universal's <i><a href="/wiki/Extinction_(2018_film)" title="Extinction (2018 film)">Extinction</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> and Warner Bros.' <i><a href="/wiki/Mowgli:_Legend_of_the_Jungle" title="Mowgli: Legend of the Jungle">Mowgli: Legend of the Jungle</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-MowgliNetflix_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MowgliNetflix-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<p>The following only applies to the United States. Listed companies may still or may not have licensing agreements with Netflix in other territories.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span></h3>
<p>In June 2018, Netflix announced a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Telltale_Games" title="Telltale Games">Telltale Games</a> to port its <a href="/wiki/Adventure_game" title="Adventure game">adventure games</a> to the service in a streaming video format. The games would be adapted to be similar to the existing interactive narrative stories that Netflix already offers, allowing simple controls through a television remote. The first such game, <i><a href="/wiki/Minecraft:_Story_Mode" title="Minecraft: Story Mode">Minecraft: Story Mode</a></i>, was expected to be released later in the year, and Telltale also received rights to produce a video game adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/Stranger_Things" title="Stranger Things">Stranger Things</a></i> for conventional gaming platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup>  In September 2018, Telltale underwent a "majority studio closure" and laid off nearly its entire staff beyond a skeleton crew of 25 employees, citing a loss of funding. Netflix stated that while the <i>Minecraft: Story Mode</i> port would go on, the company was seeking alternate options for the <i>Stranger Things</i> project.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Device_support">Device support</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Netflix-compatible_devices" title="List of Netflix-compatible devices">List of Netflix-compatible devices</a></div>
<p>Netflix can be accessed via an <a href="/wiki/Internet_browser" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet browser">internet browser</a> on PCs, while  Netflix apps are available on various platforms, including <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" class="mw-redirect" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray Disc</a> players, <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablet computers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile phones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smart_TV" title="Smart TV">smart TVs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Digital_media_player" title="Digital media player">digital media players</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Video_game_console" title="Video game console">video game consoles</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Xbox_One" title="Xbox One">Xbox One</a>, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wii_U" title="Wii U">Wii U</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a> and the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a> were formerly compatible with Netflix as well.
</p><p>In addition, a growing number of <a href="/wiki/Multichannel_television" title="Multichannel television">multichannel television</a> providers, including <a href="/wiki/Cable_television" title="Cable television">cable television</a> and <a href="/wiki/IPTV" title="IPTV">IPTV</a> services, have also added Netflix apps accessible within their own <a href="/wiki/Set-top_box" title="Set-top box">set-top boxes</a>, sometimes with the ability for its content (along with those of other online video services) to be presented within a unified search interface alongside linear television programming as an "all-in-one" solution.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>4K streaming requires a 4K-compatible device and display, both supporting <a href="/wiki/HDCP" class="mw-redirect" title="HDCP">HDCP</a> 2.2. 4K streaming on personal computers requires hardware and software support of the Microsoft <a href="/wiki/PlayReady" title="PlayReady">PlayReady</a> 3.0 <a href="/wiki/Digital_rights_management" title="Digital rights management">digital rights management</a> solution, which requires a compatible CPU, graphics card, and software environment. Currently, this feature is limited to <a href="/wiki/Kaby_Lake" title="Kaby Lake">7th generation</a> <a href="/wiki/Intel_Core" title="Intel Core">Intel Core</a> or later CPUs, <a href="/wiki/Windows_10" title="Windows 10">Windows 10</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nvidia" title="Nvidia">Nvidia</a> <a href="/wiki/Geforce_10_series" class="mw-redirect" title="Geforce 10 series">Geforce 10 series</a> and AMD <a href="/wiki/AMD_Radeon_400_series" title="AMD Radeon 400 series">Radeon 400 series</a> or later graphics cards, and running through <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Edge" title="Microsoft Edge">Microsoft Edge</a> web browser, or the Netflix <a href="/wiki/Universal_app" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal app">universal app</a> available on <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Store_(digital)" title="Microsoft Store (digital)">Microsoft Store</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pcw-playready4k_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcw-playready4k-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-techradar-4k_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techradar-4k-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ars-netflix4k_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-netflix4k-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nvidia_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nvidia-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AMD_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMD-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sales_and_marketing">Sales and marketing</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Netflix_booth_(36079051696).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Netflix_booth_%2836079051696%29.jpg/220px-Netflix_booth_%2836079051696%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Netflix_booth_%2836079051696%29.jpg/330px-Netflix_booth_%2836079051696%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Netflix_booth_%2836079051696%29.jpg/440px-Netflix_booth_%2836079051696%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="3840" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Netflix_booth_(36079051696).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Netflix's booth at the 2017 <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con" title="San Diego Comic-Con">San Diego Comic-Con</a></div></div></div>
<p>During Q1 2011, sales and rentals of DVDs and Blu-ray discs plunged about 35%, and the sell-through of packaged discs fell 19.99% to $2.07 billion, with more money spent on subscription than in-store rentals. This decrease was attributed to the rising popularity of Netflix and other streaming services.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2012, Netflix hired Kelly Bennett – former Warner Bros. Vice President of Interactive, Worldwide Marketing – to become its new Chief Marketing Officer. This also filled a vacancy at Netflix that had been empty for over six months when their previous CMO Leslie Kilgore left in January 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Netflix's website has 117.6 million subscribers as of 2018, with 8.3 million being added in the fourth quarter of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> As of January 28, 2018, Netflix's website ranked as the 30th most trafficked website in the world and 9th most trafficked website in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Netflix has a <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> feed, used to tweet about the new and upcoming shows that include <a href="/wiki/Hashtags" class="mw-redirect" title="Hashtags">hashtags</a> to encourage engagement of their audience to not only watch the show but to contribute to the hashtag themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_expansion">International expansion</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_expansion_of_Netflix" title="International expansion of Netflix">International expansion of Netflix</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Netflix_at_Thong_Lor.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Netflix_at_Thong_Lor.jpg/220px-Netflix_at_Thong_Lor.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Netflix_at_Thong_Lor.jpg/330px-Netflix_at_Thong_Lor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Netflix_at_Thong_Lor.jpg/440px-Netflix_at_Thong_Lor.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2976" data-file-height="3968" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Netflix_at_Thong_Lor.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Netflix advertising at <a href="/wiki/Thong_Lo_BTS_station" title="Thong Lo BTS station">Thong Lo BTS station</a>, Bangkok</div></div></div>

</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>2015
</th>
<td>Netflix expanded to <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Netflix_Aus_and_NZ_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Netflix_Aus_and_NZ-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Netflix_Japan_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Netflix_Japan-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>2016
</th>
<td>Netflix announced at the <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Electronics_Show" title="Consumer Electronics Show">Consumer Electronics Show</a> in January 2016 that it had become available everywhere worldwide outside of <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> and the territory of <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>2017
</th>
<td>In April 2017, Netflix confirmed it had reached a licensing deal in China for original Netflix content with <a href="/wiki/IQiyi" title="IQiyi">iQiYi</a>, a Chinese video streaming platform owned by <a href="/wiki/Baidu" title="Baidu">Baidu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>As of July 2019, Netflix officially supports 23 languages for <a href="/wiki/User_interface" title="User interface">user interface</a> and <a href="/wiki/Customer_support" title="Customer support">customer support</a> purposes: Arabic (<a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Modern Standard</a>), Chinese (<a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">Simplified</a> and <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">Traditional</a>), Danish, Dutch, English, Finnish, French, German, Greek, Hebrew, Indonesian, Italian, Japanese, Korean, Norwegian (<a href="/wiki/Bokm%C3%A5l" title="Bokmål">Bokmål</a>), Polish, Portuguese (<a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Portuguese" title="Brazilian Portuguese">Brazilian</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Portuguese" title="European Portuguese">European</a>), Romanian, Spanish (<a href="/wiki/Castilian_Spanish" title="Castilian Spanish">Castilian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_Americas" title="Spanish language in the Americas">Latin American</a>), Swahili, Swedish, Thai and Turkish.<sup id="cite_ref-Netflix_Language_Preferences_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Netflix_Language_Preferences-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Netflix has encountered political controversy for some of its international productions, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mechanism_(TV_series)" title="The Mechanism (TV series)">The Mechanism</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Fauda" title="Fauda">Fauda</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Amo_(TV_series)" title="Amo (TV series)">Amo</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> An episode of the series <i><a href="/wiki/Patriot_Act_with_Hasan_Minhaj" title="Patriot Act with Hasan Minhaj">Patriot Act with Hasan Minhaj</a></i> criticizing the Saudi Arabia government was initially available on Netflix within Saudi Arabia but was later made unavailable in the country after a legal complaint from the government.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> In India, Netflix along with its local competitor Hotstar announced plans in early 2019 to adopt self-regulation guidelines for content streamed on their platforms within the country in an effort to prevent potential implementation of government censorship laws.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> The Jordanian series <i><a href="/wiki/Jinn_(TV_series)" title="Jinn (TV series)">Jinn</a></i> was condemned by members of the country's government for contravening the country's moral standards, and the country's highest prosecutor has sought to have the series banned from streaming.<sup id="cite_ref-io9Jinn_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-io9Jinn-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 3, 2019, Netflix applied for a license to continue its streaming services in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, under the country's new broadcasting rules. The television watchdog of <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radio_and_Television_Supreme_Council" title="Radio and Television Supreme Council">Radio and Television Supreme Council</a> (RTÜK) issued new guidelines, under which content providers were required to get new license for operating in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
