<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competitors">Competitors</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Online_DVD_rental" class="mw-redirect" title="Online DVD rental">Online DVD rental</a> and <a href="/wiki/Video_on_demand" title="Video on demand">Video on demand</a></div>
<p>Netflix's success was followed by the establishment of numerous other DVD rental companies, both in the United States and abroad. <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a> began an online rental service in October 2002 but left the market in May 2005. However, Walmart later acquired the rental service <a href="/wiki/Vudu" title="Vudu">Vudu</a> in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Blockbuster_Video" class="mw-redirect" title="Blockbuster Video">Blockbuster Video</a> entered the United States online market in August 2004, with a US$19.95 monthly subscription service (equivalent to $26.46&#32;in 2018). This sparked a <a href="/wiki/Price_war" title="Price war">price war</a>; Netflix had raised its popular three-disc plan from US$19.95 to US$21.99 just prior to Blockbuster's launch, but by October, Netflix reduced this fee to US$17.99. Blockbuster responded with rates as low as US$14.99 for a time, but, by August 2005, both companies settled at identical rates.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> On July 22, 2007, Netflix dropped the prices of its two most popular plans by US$1.00 in an effort to better compete with Blockbuster's online-only offerings.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> On October 4, 2012, <a href="/wiki/Dish_Network" title="Dish Network">Dish Network</a> scrapped plans to make Blockbuster into a Netflix competitor.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> (Dish bought the ailing Blockbuster, LLC in 2011 and will continue to license the brand name to franchise locations, and keep its "Blockbuster on Demand" video streaming service open.)<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005, Netflix cited Amazon.com as a potential competitor,<sup id="cite_ref-C4WDefault-5450355_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C4WDefault-5450355-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> which until 2008, offered online video rentals in the United Kingdom and Germany. This arm of the business was eventually sold to LoveFilm; however, Amazon then bought LoveFilm in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> In addition, Amazon now streams movies and television shows through Amazon Video (formerly Amazon Video On Demand and LOVEFiLM Instant).<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Redbox" title="Redbox">Redbox</a> is another competitor that uses a <a href="/wiki/Kiosk" title="Kiosk">kiosk</a> approach: Rather than mailing DVDs, customers pick up and return DVDs at self-service kiosks located in metropolitan areas. In September 2012, <a href="/wiki/Coinstar" class="mw-redirect" title="Coinstar">Coinstar</a>, the owners of Redbox, announced plans to partner with <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Communications" title="Verizon Communications">Verizon</a> to launch <i>Redbox Instant by Verizon</i> by late 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup> In early 2013, <i>Redbox Instant by Verizon</i> began a limited beta release of its service,<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> which was described by critics as "No Netflix killer"<sup id="cite_ref-CNET_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNET-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> due to "glitches [and] lackluster selection."<sup id="cite_ref-NASDAQ_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASDAQ-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/CuriosityStream" title="CuriosityStream">CuriosityStream</a>, a premium ad-free, subscription-based service launched in March 2015 similar to Netflix but offering strictly nonfiction content in the areas of science, technology, civilization and the human spirit, has been dubbed the "new Netflix for non-fiction".<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hulu_Plus" class="mw-redirect" title="Hulu Plus">Hulu Plus</a>, like Netflix and Amazon Prime Instant Video, "ink[s] their own deals for exclusive and original content", requiring Netflix "not only to continue to attract new subscribers, but also keep existing ones happy."<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Netflix largely avoids offering <a href="/wiki/Pornography" title="Pornography">pornography</a>, but several "adult video" subscription services were inspired by Netflix, such as <a href="/wiki/SugarInstant" title="SugarInstant">SugarInstant</a> and <a href="/wiki/WantedList" title="WantedList">WantedList</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Australia, Netflix competes with several local streaming companies, most notably locally operated services <a href="/wiki/Stan_(company)" title="Stan (company)">Stan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quickflix" title="Quickflix">Quickflix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic countries</a>, Netflix competes with <a href="/wiki/Viaplay" class="mw-redirect" title="Viaplay">Viaplay</a>, <a href="/wiki/HBO_Nordic" class="mw-redirect" title="HBO Nordic">HBO Nordic</a> and <a href="/wiki/C_More" class="mw-redirect" title="C More">C More</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, Netflix competes with <a href="/wiki/HOOQ" title="HOOQ">HOOQ</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> Astro On the Go, Sky on Demand, <a href="/wiki/Singtel_TV" title="Singtel TV">Singtel TV</a>, HomeCable OnDemand, and <a href="/wiki/Iflix" title="Iflix">iflix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup> In New Zealand, Netflix competes with local streaming companies including <a href="/wiki/Television_New_Zealand" class="mw-redirect" title="Television New Zealand">Television New Zealand</a> (TVNZ),<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mediaworks_New_Zealand" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediaworks New Zealand">Mediaworks New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sky_Network_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Sky Network Television">Sky Network Television</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lightbox_(New_Zealand)" title="Lightbox (New Zealand)">Lightbox</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> Neon and <a href="/wiki/Quickflix" title="Quickflix">Quickflix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup> In Italy, Netflix competes with Infinity, <a href="/wiki/Now_TV_(Sky_plc)" class="mw-redirect" title="Now TV (Sky plc)">Now TV</a> and TIMvision.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, Netflix competes with <a href="/wiki/Showmax" title="Showmax">Showmax</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/MENA" title="MENA">MENA</a> region, Netflix competes with <a href="/wiki/Icflix" title="Icflix">icflix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starz" title="Starz">Starz Play Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/OSN" title="OSN">OSN</a>'s Wavo, and <a href="/wiki/Iflix" title="Iflix">iflix Arabia</a>. Also, in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, Netflix competes with <a href="/wiki/Rede_Globo" title="Rede Globo">Globoplay</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Grupo_Globo" title="Grupo Globo">Grupo Globo</a>'s streaming service, and <a href="/wiki/RecordTV" title="RecordTV">PlayPlus</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Grupo_Record" title="Grupo Record">Grupo Record</a>'s streaming service.
</p><p>In Mexico, <a href="/wiki/Televisa" title="Televisa">Televisa</a> removed its content from Netflix in 2016 and moved it to its own streaming service <a href="/wiki/Blim" title="Blim">Blim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a> will launch their own streaming service, <a href="/wiki/Disney%2B" title="Disney+">Disney+</a>, in November 2019. As a result, Disney content currently hosted on Netflix will begin to be phased out over the next couple of years.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents">Incidents</span></h2>
<p>In February 2019, police stormed the Netflix headquarters in Hollywood after a man with a gun was reported wandering around the premises. The buildings were placed on lockdown.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_Netflix" title="List of accolades received by Netflix">List of accolades received by Netflix</a></div>
<p>On July 18, 2013, Netflix earned the first <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award" title="Primetime Emmy Award">Primetime Emmy Award</a> nominations for original online-only <a href="/wiki/Web_television" title="Web television">web television</a> programs at the <a href="/wiki/65th_Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="65th Primetime Emmy Awards">65th Primetime Emmy Awards</a>. Three of its web series, <i>Arrested Development</i>, <i>Hemlock Grove</i> and <i>House of Cards</i>, earned a combined 14 nominations (nine for <i>House of Cards</i>, three for <i>Arrested Development</i> and two for <i>Hemlock Grove</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-NDWi2PEN_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NDWi2PEN-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup> The <i>House of Cards</i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Chapter_1_(House_of_Cards)" title="Chapter 1 (House of Cards)">Chapter 1</a>" received four nominations for both the 65th Primetime Emmy Awards and <a href="/wiki/65th_Primetime_Creative_Arts_Emmy_Awards" title="65th Primetime Creative Arts Emmy Awards">65th Primetime Creative Arts Emmy Awards</a>, becoming the first <a href="/wiki/Webisode" title="Webisode">webisode</a> of a television series to receive a major Primetime Emmy Award nomination: David Fincher was nominated in the category of Outstanding Directing for a Drama Series.<sup id="cite_ref-NDWi2PEN_316-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NDWi2PEN-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup> "Chapter 1" joined <i>Arrested Development</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> "<a href="/wiki/Flight_of_the_Phoenix_(Arrested_Development)" title="Flight of the Phoenix (Arrested Development)">Flight of the Phoenix</a>" and <i>Hemlock Grove</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> "Children of the Night" as the first webisodes to earn Creative Arts Emmy Award nomination, and with its win for Outstanding Cinematography for a Single-Camera Series, "Chapter 1" became the first webisode to be awarded an Emmy.<sup id="cite_ref-NMHWTPCAEA_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NMHWTPCAEA-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup> Fincher's win for Directing for a Drama Series made the episode the first Primetime Emmy-awarded webisode.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 12, 2013, the network earned six <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Awards" title="Golden Globe Awards">Golden Globe Award</a> nominations, including four for <i>House of Cards</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> Among those nominations was Wright for <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actress_%E2%80%93_Television_Series_Drama" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actress – Television Series Drama">Golden Globe Award for Best Actress – Television Series Drama</a> for her portrayal of Claire Underwood, which she won at the <a href="/wiki/71st_Golden_Globe_Awards" title="71st Golden Globe Awards">71st Golden Globe Awards</a> on January 12. With the accolade, Wright became the first actress to win a Golden Globe for an online-only web television series. It also marked Netflix' first major acting award.<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> <i>House of Cards</i> and <i>Orange is the New Black</i> also won <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Peabody Awards">Peabody Awards</a> in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 10, 2014, Netflix received 31 Emmy nominations. Among other nominations, <i>House of Cards</i> received nominations for Outstanding Drama Series, Outstanding Directing in a Drama Series and Outstanding Writing in a Drama Series. Kevin Spacey and Robin Wright were nominated for Outstanding Lead Actor and Outstanding Lead Actress in a Drama Series. <i>Orange is the New Black</i> was nominated in the comedy categories, earning nominations for Outstanding Comedy Series, Outstanding Writing For A Comedy Series and Outstanding Directing For A Comedy Series. Taylor Schilling, Kate Mulgrew and Uzo Aduba were respectively nominated for Outstanding Lead Actress in a Comedy Series, Outstanding Supporting Actress in a Comedy Series and Outstanding Guest Actress in a Comedy Series (the latter was for Aduba's recurring role in season one, as she was promoted to series regular for the show's second season).<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Netflix got the largest share of 2016 Emmy award nominations among its competitors, with 16 major nominations. However, streaming shows only got 24 nominations out of a total of 139, falling significantly behind cable.<sup id="cite_ref-digitaljournal.com_326-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-digitaljournal.com-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup> The 16 Netflix nominees were: <i>House of Cards</i> with Kevin Spacey, <i>A Very Murray Christmas</i> with Bill Murray, <i>Unbreakable Kimmy Schmidt</i>, <i>Master of None</i>, and <i>Bloodline</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-digitaljournal.com_326-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-digitaljournal.com-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Stranger Things</i> received 19 nominations at the <a href="/wiki/69th_Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="69th Primetime Emmy Awards">2017 Primetime Emmy Awards</a>, while <i><a href="/wiki/The_Crown_(TV_series)" title="The Crown (TV series)">The Crown</a></i> received 13 nominations.<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2017, Netflix was nominated for Broadcaster of the Year in the UK's Diversity in Media Awards.
</p><p>In December 2017, Netflix was awarded <a href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals" title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals">PETA</a>'s Company of the Year for promoting animal rights movies and documentaries like <i><a href="/wiki/Forks_Over_Knives" title="Forks Over Knives">Forks Over Knives</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/What_the_Health" title="What the Health">What the Health</a></i>.
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/90th_Academy_Awards" title="90th Academy Awards">90th Academy Awards</a>, held on March 4, 2018, Netflix won the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Documentary_Feature" title="Academy Award for Best Documentary Feature">Oscar for Best Documentary Feature</a> for the film <i><a href="/wiki/Icarus_(2017_film)" title="Icarus (2017 film)">Icarus</a>.</i> During his remarks backstage, director and writer Bryan Fogel remarked that Netflix had "single-handedly changed the documentary world." <i>Icarus</i> had its premiere at the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Sundance_Film_Festival" title="Sundance Film Festival">Sundance Film Festival</a> and was bought by Netflix for $5 million, one of the biggest deals ever for a non-fiction film.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Netflix became the most nominated network at the 2018 <a href="/wiki/70th_Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="70th Primetime Emmy Awards">Primetime</a> and <a href="/wiki/70th_Primetime_Creative_Arts_Emmy_Awards" title="70th Primetime Creative Arts Emmy Awards">Creative Arts Emmy Awards</a> with 112 nominations, therefore breaking <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a>'s 17-years record as most nominated network at the Emmys, who received 108 nominations.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 22, 2019, Netflix scored 15 nominations for the <a href="/wiki/91st_Academy_Awards" title="91st Academy Awards">91st Academy Awards</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture" title="Academy Award for Best Picture">Best Picture</a> for <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Cuar%C3%B3n" title="Alfonso Cuarón">Alfonso Cuarón</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Roma_(2018_film)" title="Roma (2018 film)">Roma</a></i>, which was nominated for 10 awards.<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup> The 15 nominations equal the total nominations Netflix had received in previous years. Its increased presence in the Academy Awards has led filmmakers such as <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a> to speak out against the nomination of streaming content. As a possible solution, Netflix is in the process of buying <a href="/wiki/Grauman%27s_Egyptian_Theatre" title="Grauman&#39;s Egyptian Theatre">Grauman's Egyptian Theatre</a> to host events and screen its films and series.<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup> However, there are no plans to roll out full theatrical releases there.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance_and_revenue">Finance and revenue</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010">2010</span></h3>
<p>In 2010, Netflix's stock price increased 219% to $175.70 and it added eight million subscribers, bringing its total to 20 million. Revenue jumped 29% to $2.16 billion and net income was up 39% to $161 million.<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011">2011</span></h3>
<p>In April 2011, Netflix was expected to earn $1.07 a share in the first quarter of 2011 on revenue of $705.7 million, a huge increase compared to the year-earlier profit of 59¢ on revenue of $493.7 million, according to a survey of 25 analysts polled by FactSet Research.<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At their peak, in July 2011, Netflix shares were trading for $299. Following the customer dissatisfaction and resulting loss of subscribers after the announcements by CEO Hastings that streaming and DVD rental would be charged separately, leading to a higher price for customers who wanted both (on September 1), and that the DVD rental would be split off as the subsidiary Qwikster (on September 18), the share price fell steeply, to around $130.<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup> However, on October 10, 2011, plans to split the company were scrapped. The reason being that "two websites would make things more difficult", he stated on the Netflix blog. On November 22, Netflix's share tumbled, as share prices fell by as much as 7%.<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup> By December 2011, as a consequence of its decision to raise prices, Netflix had lost over 75% of its total value from the summer.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup> Describing their business model as "broken", Wedbush downgraded Netflix's stock rating to "underperform", the equivalent of sell.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014">2014</span></h3>
<p>In May 2014, Netflix increased the fee for UK subscribers by £1.<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup> The price increase took effect immediately for new subscribers, but would be delayed for two years for existing members. Netflix applied similar increases in the United States (an increase of $1) and the Eurozone (an increase of €1). According to <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Forbes (magazine)">Forbes</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup> "Netflix can add roughly $500 million in annual incremental revenues in the U.S. alone by 2017 with this move" and "roughly $200–250 million in incremental revenues from price changes in international markets". However, Reuters' Felix Salmon is critical about Netflix's financial future, noting that "any time that Netflix builds up a profit margin, the studios will simply raise their prices until that margin disappears".<sup id="cite_ref-Problem_344-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Problem-344">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016">2016</span></h3>
<p>In April 2016, Netflix announced it would be ending a loyalty rate in certain countries for subscribers who were continuously subscribed before price rises.<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup> Netflix spent about $5 billion on original content in 2016;<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup> this compares to a 2015 revenue of US$6.77 billion (2015).<sup id="cite_ref-FY_347-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FY-347">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Netflix" title="Criticism of Netflix">Criticism of Netflix</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_distribution_model">Film distribution model</span></h3>
<p>Netflix's distribution model for original films has led to conflicts with the legacy film industry. Some cinemas have refused to screen films distributed theatrically by Netflix (primarily to ensure awards eligibility), as it defies the standard three-month <a href="/wiki/Release_window" class="mw-redirect" title="Release window">release window</a>, and releases them simultaneously on its streaming platform (although <i><a href="/wiki/Roma_(2018_film)" title="Roma (2018 film)">Roma</a></i> was instead given a three-week run before being added to the streaming service). <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a>—governor of the directors branch of the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Motion_Picture_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences">Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences</a> (AMPAS), has been critical of the streaming model over the "communal", cinema experience, but later clarified his views by arguing that viewers should have access to "great stories", and be able to "find their entertainment in any form or fashion that suits them."<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup> In April 2019, AMPAS voted against the possibility of changes to the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a> eligibility criteria to account for streaming services such as Netflix, although AMPAS president <a href="/wiki/John_Bailey_(cinematographer)" title="John Bailey (cinematographer)">John Bailey</a> did state that the organization would "further study the profound changes occurring in our industry".<sup id="cite_ref-screendaily-eligibility_352-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-screendaily-eligibility-352">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, Netflix pulled out of the <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival" title="Cannes Film Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a>, in response to new rules requiring competition films to have been released in French theaters. The Cannes premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/Okja" title="Okja">Okja</a></i>  in 2017 was controversial, and led to discussions over the appropriateness of films with simultaneous digital releases being screened at an event showcasing theatrical film; audience members also booed at the Netflix <a href="/wiki/Vanity_plate" title="Vanity plate">vanity plate</a> at the screening. Netflix's attempts to negotiate allowing a limited release in France were curtailed by organizers, as well as French law—where theatrically screened films are legally banned from being made available via video on-demand services until at least 36 months after their release.<sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Beginning at the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="Toronto International Film Festival">Toronto International Film Festival</a>, films may now be restricted from screening at <a href="/wiki/Scotiabank_Theatre_Toronto" title="Scotiabank Theatre Toronto">Scotiabank Theatre Toronto</a>—one of the festival's main venues—and screened elsewhere (such as <a href="/wiki/TIFF_Bell_Lightbox" title="TIFF Bell Lightbox">TIFF Bell Lightbox</a> and other local cinemas) if distributed by a service such as Netflix. Organizers stated that the restriction was due to a policy enforced by the facility's owner and operator, <a href="/wiki/Cineplex_Entertainment" title="Cineplex Entertainment">Cineplex Entertainment</a>, requiring adherence to 3-month theatrical windows.<sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Content_and_partnerships">Content and partnerships</span></h3>
<p>Individual Netflix productions have also faced controversy over their content. Critics argued that <i><a href="/wiki/13_Reasons_Why" title="13 Reasons Why">13 Reasons Why</a></i> glamorized mental health issues such as <a href="/wiki/Suicide" title="Suicide">suicide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Depression_in_childhood_and_adolescence" title="Depression in childhood and adolescence">depression</a> and <a href="/wiki/Posttraumatic_stress_disorder" title="Posttraumatic stress disorder">post-traumatic stress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, Netflix was criticized for using stock footage from the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Lac-M%C3%A9gantic_rail_disaster" title="Lac-Mégantic rail disaster">Lac-Mégantic rail disaster</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Bird_Box_(film)" title="Bird Box (film)">Bird Box</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Travelers_(TV_series)" title="Travelers (TV series)">Travelers</a></i>. The footage was subsequently replaced.<sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup> In January 2019, Netflix censored an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Patriot_Act_with_Hasan_Minhaj" title="Patriot Act with Hasan Minhaj">Patriot Act with Hasan Minhaj</a></i> in Saudi Arabia after requests by the <a href="/wiki/Communications_and_Information_Technology_Commission_(Saudi_Arabia)" title="Communications and Information Technology Commission (Saudi Arabia)">Communications and Information Technology Commission</a>, citing material critical of the country (such as <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_bin_Salman" title="Mohammad bin Salman">Mohammad bin Salman</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi-led military campaign in Yemen</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The announcement that <a href="/wiki/Gwyneth_Paltrow" title="Gwyneth Paltrow">Gwyneth Paltrow</a>'s company <a href="/wiki/Goop_(company)" title="Goop (company)">Goop</a> had partnered with Netflix led to criticism, noting that the company has frequently been criticized for making unsubstantiated claims about the effectiveness of health treatments and products that it promotes. Multiple critics argued that granting Goop access to Netflix's platform was a "win for <a href="/wiki/Pseudoscience" title="Pseudoscience">pseudoscience</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bundel_364-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bundel-364">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ars-goopseries_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-goopseries-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accessibility">Accessibility</span></h3>
<p>In 2011, Netflix was sued by the <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_the_Deaf_(United_States)" title="National Association of the Deaf (United States)">U.S. National Association of the Deaf</a> for not providing <a href="/wiki/Closed_captioning" title="Closed captioning">captioning</a> for the deaf or hard of hearing on all of its content, citing the <a href="/wiki/Americans_with_Disabilities_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Americans with Disabilities Act">Americans with Disabilities Act</a>. Netflix later agreed to a settlement, where it would caption its entire library by 2014, and by 2016, have captioning available for new content within seven days of release.<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup> In an <a href="/wiki/Non-publication_of_legal_opinions_in_the_United_States" title="Non-publication of legal opinions in the United States">unpublished decision</a> issued 2015, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Ninth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit">Ninth Circuit Court of Appeals</a> ruled that the ADA did not apply to Netflix in this case, as it is "not connected to any actual, physical place".<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup> Netflix has continued to face criticism from disability rights supporters over the quality of captioning on some of its content.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">&#91;367&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">&#91;368&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Viewership_figure_claims">Viewership figure claims</span></h3>
<p>Netflix has been called out by some media organizations and competitors for only rarely and selectively releasing its ratings and viewer numbers. A notable instance of this involves the film <i><a href="/wiki/Bird_Box_(film)" title="Bird Box (film)">Bird Box</a></i>. A week after its release, Netflix claimed that it had the biggest seven-day viewing record of any of its original films at over 45 million viewers, but did not provide data to validate it.<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">&#91;369&#93;</a></sup> It also wasn't possible to accurately compare its week-long success to a major cultural event such as the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a> or <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a> or to a <a href="/wiki/Blockbuster_(entertainment)" title="Blockbuster (entertainment)">blockbuster</a> film run.<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup> In June 2019, Netflix claimed that 30,869,863 accounts watched the <a href="/wiki/Adam_Sandler" title="Adam Sandler">Adam Sandler</a>- and <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Aniston" title="Jennifer Aniston">Jennifer Aniston</a>-starring Netflix original film <i><a href="/wiki/Murder_Mystery_(film)" title="Murder Mystery (film)">Murder Mystery</a></i>, despite it being critically panned, making it the biggest "opening weekend" for a Netflix original film. If the film had been in theaters it would have made the equivalent of $556 million based on a $9 ticket price. Critics cast doubt that this amount of people would have watched the film given that it would have made the film more popular than the finale of <i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones" title="Game of Thrones">Game of Thrones</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_and_legacy">Effects and legacy</span></h2>
<p>The rise of Netflix has affected the way that audiences watch televised content. Netflix's CPO Neil Hunt points out that the Internet allows users the freedom to watch shows at their own pace, so an episode does not need cliffhangers to tease the audience to keep tuning in week after week because they can just continue into the next episode.<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup> Netflix has allowed content creators to deviate from traditional formats that force 30 minute or 60 minute time slots once a week, which it claims gives them an advantage over networks. Their model provides a platform which allows varying run times per episode based on a storyline, eliminates the need for a week to week recap, and does not have a fixed notion of what constitutes a "season". This flexibility also allows Netflix to nurture a show until it finds its audience, unlike traditional networks which will quickly cancel a show if it is unable to maintain steady ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Netflix has strayed from the traditional necessary production of a pilot episode in order to establish the characters and create arbitrary cliffhangers to prove to the network that the concept of the show will be successful. Kevin Spacey spoke at the <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_International_Television_Festival" title="Edinburgh International Television Festival">Edinburgh International Television Festival</a> about how the new Netflix model was effective for the production of <i>House of Cards</i>: "Netflix was the only company that said, 'We believe in you. We've run our data, and it tells us our audience would watch this series.'" Traditional networks are unwilling to risk millions of dollars on shows without first seeing a pilot, but Spacey points out that 113 pilots were made in 2012; 35 of them were chosen to go to air, 13 were renewed, and most are gone now. The total cost of this is somewhere between $300 million and $400 million, which makes Netflix's deal for <i>House of Cards</i> extremely cost effective, according to Spacey.<sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">&#91;374&#93;</a></sup> Netflix's subscription fee also eliminates the need for commercials, so they do not need to appease advertisers to fund their original content, a model similar to pay television services such as HBO and Showtime.
</p><p>The Netflix model has also affected viewers' expectations. According to a 2013 Nielsen survey, more than 60-percent of Americans said that they binge-watch shows, and nearly 8 out of 10 Americans have used technology to watch their favorite shows on their own schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">&#91;375&#93;</a></sup> Netflix has continued to release its original content by making the whole season available at once, acknowledging changing viewer habits. This allows audiences to watch episodes at a time of their choosing rather than having to watch just one episode a week at a specific scheduled time; this effectively gives its subscribers freedom and control over when to watch the next episode at their own pace.
</p><p>In June 2016, Russian Minister of Culture <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Medinsky" title="Vladimir Medinsky">Vladimir Medinsky</a> asserted that Netflix is part of a US government plot to influence the world culture, "to enter every home, get into every television, and through that television, into the head of every person on earth". This was part of his argument for the increase of funding of Russian cinema to pitch it against the dominance of Hollywood.<sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
